Since \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E\) is dense in \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) by Theorem 1.3.6, we have to verify that \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) induces on \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E\) the projective topology.

Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal E},{\cal S},{\cal O}_{M}\}\) and let \(p\) be one of the seminorms (1.1.3), (1.1.7), or (1.1.9), respectively. Then

\[p(\varphi\otimes e)=p(\varphi)\left|e\right|\ ,\qquad\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X) \ ,\quad e\in E\ ,\]

where on the left side \(p\) is the seminorm on \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\), and on the right side \(p\) denotes the corresponding seminorm on \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\). From this we easily deduce that \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) induces on \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E\) a topology that is weaker than the projective tensor product topology.

---

Conversely, let \(\sum\varphi_{j}\otimes e_{j}\) be a representation of \(z\in\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E\). Then, given \(\varphi^{\prime}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\) and \(e^{\prime}\in E^{\prime}\),

\[\sum\langle\varphi^{\prime},\varphi_{j}\rangle\langle e^{\prime},e_{j}\rangle= \left\langle e^{\prime},\sum\langle\varphi^{\prime},\varphi_{j}\rangle e_{j} \right\rangle=\left\langle e^{\prime},\left\langle\varphi^{\prime},\sum\varphi_ {j}\otimes e_{j}\right\rangle\right\rangle\,.\]

Consequently (cf. (1.4.7)),

\[p\otimes_{\varepsilon}|\cdot|_{E}(z)=\sup_{\varphi^{\prime}\in\mathbb{R}^{0}_{ p}}|\langle\varphi^{\prime},z\rangle|_{E}\leq p(z)\]

by the bipolar theorem. This shows that the topology induced by \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) on \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E\) is stronger than the injective tensor product topology. Since \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\) is nuclear, the latter coincides with the projective topology.

Finally, given \(K\subset\subset X\), the last string of arguments shows that \(\mathcal{D}_{K}(X,E)\) induces on \(\mathcal{D}_{K}(X)\otimes E\) the projective topology. Since \(\mathcal{D}(X,E)\) induces on \(\mathcal{D}_{K}(X,E)\) its original topology, it follows that \(\mathcal{D}(X,E)\) induces on \(\mathcal{D}_{K}(X)\otimes E\) the projective topology. From

\[\mathcal{D}(X)\otimes E=\varinjlim_{K\subset\subset X}\mathcal{D}_{K}(X)\otimes E\]

(e.g., [1, Corollary 4 to Theorem 15.5.3]) it follows that \(\mathcal{D}(X,E)\) induces on \(\mathcal{D}(X)\otimes E\) the projective tensor product topology. Thus, since \(\mathcal{D}(X)\otimes E\) is dense in \(\mathcal{D}(X,E)\) by Theorem 1.3.6, it follows that \(\mathcal{D}(X)\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E=\mathcal{D}(X,E)\).

Suppose that \(F\) and \(G\) are Frechet spaces such that \(F\) is nuclear. Then

\[(F\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}G)^{\prime}=F^{\prime}\stackrel{{ \sim}}{{\otimes}}G^{\prime}\] (1.4.16)

by means of the duality pairing induced by

\[\langle f^{\prime}\otimes g^{\prime},f\otimes g\rangle:=\langle f^{\prime},f \rangle\langle g^{\prime},g\rangle\;,\qquad(f,g)\in F\times G\;,\quad(f^{ \prime},g^{\prime})\in F^{\prime}\times G^{\prime}\;,\] (1.4.17)

(e.g., [2, Theorem IV.9.9]). By means of this fact we can identify the dual of \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) for \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{E},\mathcal{S}\}\).

**1.4.10 Corollary**: _Let \(E\) be a Banach space and suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{E},\mathcal{E}^{\prime},\mathcal{S},\mathcal{S}^{ \prime}\}\). Then_

\[\mathfrak{F}(X,E)^{\prime}=\left(\mathfrak{F}(X)\stackrel{{\sim}} {{\otimes}}E\right)^{\prime}=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\stackrel{{ \sim}}{{\otimes}}E^{\prime}=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X,E^{\prime})\]

_by means of the duality pairing induced by (1.4.17). If \(E\) is reflexive then \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) is reflexive as well._

There are various versions of the abstract kernel theorem in the textbook literature (e.g., [1, Theorem 21.5.9], [2, Section 50]). However, it is always assumed that \(F\) and \(G\) are Frechet spaces. Since we need to apply Theorem 1.4.8 in the special case that \(F=\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) and since \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) is not metrizable, this assumption does not fit our purposes. For this reason we have included a complete proof of Theorem 1.4.8.

---

### Extending Bilinear Maps

In this subsection we prove a general extension theorem for bilinear maps on tensor products. For this we need a technical lemma guaranteeing a suitable kind of uniformity for equicontinuous sets of nuclear maps.

#### 1.5.1 Lemma

_Let \(F\) be a nuclear LCS and \(E\) a Banach space. Suppose that \(\mathcal{T}\) is an equicontinuous subset of \(\mathcal{L}(F,E)\). Then there exist a summable sequence \((\lambda_{j})\) in \(\mathbb{K}\), an equicontinuous sequence \((f^{\prime}_{j})\) in \(F^{\prime}\), and a bounded map_

\[\mathcal{T}\to B(\mathbb{N},E)\ ,\quad T\mapsto\big{(}e_{j}(T)\big{)}_{j\in \mathbb{N}}\]

_such that_

\[Tf=\sum_{j}\lambda_{j}\langle f^{\prime}_{j},f\rangle e_{j}(T)\ ,\qquad f\in F\ , \quad T\in\mathcal{T}\ .\]

ProofBy the equicontinuity of \(\mathcal{T}\), the set \(\bigcap\{\,T^{-1}(\bar{\mathbb{B}}_{E})\ ;\ T\in\mathcal{T}\,\}\) is a closed absolutely convex neighborhood of zero. Let \(p\) be its Minkowski functional. Then \(p\) is a continuous seminorm on \(F\) and

\[|Tf|_{E}\leq p(f)\ ,\qquad f\in F\ ,\quad T\in\mathcal{T}\ .\] (1.5.1)

The nuclearity of \(F\) implies, thanks to Lemma 1.4.5, the existence of a continuous seminorm \(q\geq p\) on \(F\) such that the canonical map \(S:\ F_{q}\to\widetilde{F}_{p}\) is nuclear. Hence there exist a summable sequence \((\lambda_{j})\) in \(\mathbb{K}\) and bounded sequences \(\big{(}\widehat{f}^{\prime}_{j}\big{)}\) and \((\widehat{g}_{j})\) in \((F_{q})^{\prime}\) and \(\widetilde{F}_{p}\), respectively, such that

\[S\widehat{f}=\sum_{j}\lambda_{j}\big{\langle}\widehat{f}^{\prime}_{j},\widehat {f}\big{\rangle}\widehat{g}_{j}\ ,\qquad\widehat{f}\in F_{q}\ .\] (1.5.2)

It is easy to verify that for each \(T\in\mathcal{T}\) there exists \(\widetilde{T}\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\widetilde{F}_{p},E\big{)}\) such that the diagram

is commutative, where \(\pi_{q}\) is the quotient map. Hence, letting \(f^{\prime}_{j}:=(\pi_{q})^{\prime}\widehat{f}^{\prime}_{j}\) and \(e_{j}(T):=\widetilde{T}\widehat{g}_{j}\), the assertion follows since (1.5.1) and (1.4.8) imply \(\big{\|}\widetilde{T}\big{\|}\leq 1\).

Now we are in a position to prove the following general extension theorem for bilinear maps. Throughout the remainder of this subsection we assume that \(E_{j}\)

---

\(j=0,1,2\), are Banach spaces and

\[E_{1}\times E_{2}\to E_{0}\ ,\quad(e_{1},e_{2})\mapsto e_{1}\bullet e_{2}\] (1.5.3)

is a multiplication. Furthermore, given an LCS \(F\), we put \(F(E):={\cal L}(F^{\prime},E)\) and we remind the reader of the definition of point-wise multiplication in Subsection II.1.1 of [10].

**1.5.2 Proposition**.: _Let \(F_{j}\), \(j=0,1,2\), be LCSs such that_

* \(F_{1}\) _is reflexive, complete, nuclear, and conuclear;_
* \(F_{0}(E_{0})\) _is complete._

_Suppose that there is given a hypocontinuous bilinear map_

\[F_{1}\times F_{2}(E_{2})\to F_{0}(E_{2})\ ,\quad(f_{1},v)\mapsto f_{1}\boxdot v\ .\] (1.5.4)

_Define a bilinear map_

\[\boxdot_{\bullet}\,:\,(F_{1}\otimes E_{1})\times F_{2}(E_{2})\to F_{0}(E_{0})\]

_by_

\[(f_{1}\otimes e_{1},v)\mapsto e_{1}\bullet(f_{1}\boxdot v)\ ,\qquad(e_{1},f_{1}) \in E_{1}\times F_{1}\ ,\] (1.5.5)

_and by bilinear extension otherwise. Then \(\boxdot_{\bullet}\) possesses a unique hypocontinuous bilinear extension_

\[\boxdot_{\bullet}\,:\,(F_{1}\,\,\widetilde{\otimes}\,E_{1})\times F_{2}(E_{2} )\to F_{0}(E_{0})\ ,\quad(u,v)\mapsto u\boxdot_{\bullet}v\ .\]

Proof.: Uniqueness follows immediately from the density of \(F_{1}\otimes E_{1}\) in \(F_{1}\,\,\widetilde{\otimes}\,E_{1}\).

Given \(u:=\sum f_{j}\otimes e_{j}\in F_{1}\otimes E_{1}\) and \(v\in F_{2}(E_{2})\),

\[u\boxdot_{\bullet}v=\sum e_{j}\bullet(f_{j}\boxdot v)\in F_{0}(E_{0})\ .\] (1.5.6)

Let \(B^{\prime}_{0}\) be a bounded subset of \(F^{\prime}_{0}\). Then

\[p(w):=\sup_{f^{\prime}\,\in\,B^{\prime}_{0}}|wf^{\prime}|_{E_{0}}\ ,\qquad w \in F_{0}(E_{0})\ ,\]

and

\[p_{2}(v):=\sup_{f^{\prime}\,\in\,B^{\prime}_{0}}|vf^{\prime}|_{E_{2}}\ ,\qquad v \in F_{0}(E_{2})\ ,\]

define continuous seminorms on \(F_{0}(E_{0})\) and \(F_{0}(E_{2})\), respectively. Hence

\[p(u\boxdot_{\bullet}v)\leq\sum_{j}p_{2}(f_{j}\boxdot v)\,|e_{j}|_{E_{1}}\ .\] (1.5.7)

---

Let \(B_{2}\) be a bounded subset of \(F_{2}(E_{2})\). Then (1.5.7) and the hypocontinuity of (1.5.4) imply the existence of a continuous seminorm \(p_{1}\) on \(F_{1}\) such that

\[p(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v)\leq\sum_{j}p_{1}(f_{j})\left|e_{j}\right| _{E_{1}}\ ,\qquad v\in B_{2}\ .\]

Since \(p_{1}\) is independent of the particular representation of \(u\), it follows that

\[p(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v)\leq(p_{1}\otimes_{\pi}\left|\cdot\right| )(u)\ ,\qquad u\in F_{1}\otimes E_{1}\ ,\quad v\in B_{2}\ .\]

This shows that

\[(u\mapsto u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v)\in{\cal L}\bigl{(}F_{1} \otimes_{\pi}E_{1},F_{0}(E_{0})\bigr{)}\ ,\]

uniformly with respect to \(v\) in bounded subsets of \(F_{2}(E_{2})\).

Given \(v\in F_{2}(E_{2})\), there exists a unique continuous extension

\[U_{v}\in{\cal L}\bigl{(}F_{1}\buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1},F_{0}(E_{0}) \bigr{)}\]

of (1.5.8), thanks to assumption (ii). Then

\[[(u,v)\mapsto u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v:=U_{v}(u)]\ :\ (F_{1} \buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1})\times F_{2}(E_{2})\to F_{0}(E_{0})\]

is an extension of (1.5.5) that is trivially linear in the first variable. For \(u\in F_{1}\buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1}\) choose a net \((u_{\alpha})\) in \(F_{1}\otimes E_{1}\) such that \(u_{\alpha}\to u\) in \(F_{1}\buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1}\). Then, given \(\lambda_{j}\in{\tenmsb K}\) and \(v_{j}\in F_{2}(E_{2})\) for \(j=1,2\),

\[\eqalign{u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,(\lambda_{1}v_{1}+\lambda_{2}v_{2})& =\lim_{\alpha}\bigl{[}u_{\alpha}\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,(\lambda_{1}v_{1}+ \lambda_{2}v_{2})\bigr{]}\cr&=\lambda_{1}\lim_{\alpha}(u_{\alpha}\,\mathchar 1027 \relax_{\bullet}\,v_{1})+\lambda_{2}\lim_{\alpha}(u_{\alpha}\,\mathchar 1027 \relax_{\bullet}\,v_{2})\cr&=\lambda_{1}(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v_{1})+ \lambda_{2}(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v_{2})\ .\cr}\]

Thus (1.5.10) is bilinear and it remains to show that it is hypocontinuous.

The uniformity assertion contained in (1.5.8) implies that the family of linear operators (1.5.8) is equicontinuous if \(v\) stays in bounded subsets of \(F_{2}(E_{2})\). Thus, given a closed neighborhood \(V_{0}\) of zero in \(F_{0}(E_{0})\) and a bounded subset \(B_{2}\) of \(F_{2}(E_{2})\), there exists a neighborhood \(V_{1}\) of zero in \(F_{1}\otimes_{\pi}E_{1}\) such that \(u\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v\in V_{0}\) for \((u,v)\in V_{1}\times B_{2}\). Consequently,

\[U_{v}(\overline{V}_{1})\subset V_{0}\ ,\qquad v\in B_{2}\ ,\]

where \(\overline{V}_{1}\) is the closure of \(V_{1}\) in \(F_{1}\buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1}\). This shows that \(\{\,U_{v}\ ;\,v\in B_{2}\,\}\) is equicontinuous in \({\cal L}\bigl{(}F_{1}\buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1},F_{0}(E_{0})\bigr{)}\). Hence \(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}\,v\to 0\) in \(F_{0}(E_{0})\) as \(u\to 0\) in \(F_{1}\buildrel\sim\over{\otimes}E_{1}\), uniformly with respect to \(v\) in bounded subsets of \(F_{2}(E_{2})\).

---

Now let \(B\) be a bounded subset of \(F_{1}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{1}\). Thanks to assumption (i) and Theorem 1.4.8,

\[F_{1}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{1}\cong{\cal L}(F_{1}^{\prime}, E_{1})=F_{1}(E_{1})\ .\] (1.5.11)

Put \(B_{1}\mathrel{\mathop{:}}=\tau(B)\), where \(\tau\) is the isomorphism of (1.5.11). Then \(B_{1}\) is bounded in \(F_{1}(E_{1})\). Since \(F_{1}^{\prime}\) is barreled, being the dual of a reflexive space, hence reflexive, the uniform boundedness principle shows that \(B_{1}\) is equicontinuous. Thus Lemma 1.5.1 guarantees the existence of a summable sequence \((\lambda_{j})\) in \({\mathbb{K}}\), a bounded sequence \((f_{j})\) in \(F_{1}\), and a bounded set \(C\) in \(E_{1}\) such that each \(u\in B_{1}\) has a representation \(u=\sum_{j}\lambda_{j}f_{j}\otimes e_{j}\), where \(e_{j}\in C\) and the series converges in \(F_{1}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{1}\). Hence, given \(v\in F_{2}(E_{2})\), it follows from (1.5.9), (1.5.10), and (1.5.6) that

\[u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}v=\sum_{j}\lambda_{j}e_{j}\bullet(f_{j}\, \mathchar 1027\relax v)\ .\]

Consequently,

\[p(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}v)\leq\sum_{j}|\lambda_{j}|\,p_{2}(f_{j}\, \mathchar 1027\relax v)\,|e_{j}|_{E_{1}}\ \ .\] (1.5.12)

From the hypocontinuity of (1.5.4) and the boundedness of the sequence \((f_{j})\) in \(F_{1}\) we deduce the existence of a continuous seminorm \(q\) on \(F_{2}(E_{2})\) such that

\[p_{2}(f_{j}\,\mathchar 1027\relax v)\leq q(v)\ ,\qquad v\in F_{2}(E_{2})\ ,\quad j \in{\mathbb{N}}\ .\] (1.5.13)

Since \(e_{j}\in C\) and \(C\) is bounded in \(E_{1}\), we infer from (1.5.12) and (1.5.13) that

\[p(u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}v)\leq cq(v)\ ,\qquad v\in F_{2}(E_{2})\ , \quad u\in B_{1}\ .\]

This proves that

\[(v\mapsto u\,\mathchar 1027\relax_{\bullet}v)\in{\cal L}\bigl{(}F_{2}(E_{2}),F_{ 0}(E_{0})\bigr{)}\ ,\]

uniformly with respect to \(u\) in bounded subsets of \(F_{1}\,\mathchar 1027\relax\,E_{1}\). Thus the map (1.5.10) is hypocontinuous.

By specializing we deduce from the preceding proposition the following fundamental extension result:

**1.5.3 Theorem** _Let \(F_{j}\), \(j=0,1,2\), be reflexive, complete, nuclear, and nuclear LCSs. Suppose that there are a bilinear map_

\[F_{1}\times F_{2}\to F_{0}\ ,\quad(f_{1},f_{2})\mapsto f_{1}\odot f_{2}\] (1.5.14)

_and a hypocontinuos bilinear map_

\[F_{1}\times(F_{2}\,\mathchar 1027\relax\,E_{2})\to F_{0}\,\mathchar 1027 \relax\,E_{2}\ ,\quad(f_{1},v)\mapsto f_{1}\,\hbox to 0.0pt{$\circ$}v\] (1.5.15)

---

_such that_

\[f_{1}\odot(f_{2}\otimes e_{2})=(f_{1}\odot f_{2})\otimes e_{2}\ ,\qquad f_{j}\in F _{j}\ ,\quad j=1,2\ ,\quad e_{2}\in E_{2}\ .\]

_Then there exists a unique hypocontiuous bilinear map_

\[\odot_{\bullet}\,:\ (F_{1}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{1})\times( F_{2}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{2})\to F_{0}\stackrel{{ \sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{0}\ ,\quad(u,v)\mapsto u\odot_{\bullet}v\]

_satisfying_

\[(f_{1}\otimes e_{1})\odot_{\bullet}(f_{2}\otimes e_{2})=(f_{1}\odot f_{2}) \otimes(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\]

_for \(f_{j}\in F_{j}\) and \(e_{j}\in E_{j}\), \(j=1,2\)._

**Proof** Since \(E_{j}\otimes F_{j}\) is dense in \(E_{j}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}F_{j}\) for \(j=1,2\), there exists at most one separately continuous bilinear map \(\odot_{\bullet}\) from \((F_{1}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{1})\times(F_{2}\stackrel{{ \sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{2})\) to \(F_{0}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{0}\) satisfying (1.5.18).

Thanks to Theorem 1.4.8 we can identify \(F_{j}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{j}\) with \(F_{j}(E_{j})\) by means of the respective canonical isomorphisms. Then it follows from (1.5.16) that, given \(f_{0}^{\prime}\in F_{0}^{\prime}\) and \(v:=f_{2}\otimes e_{2}\in F_{2}\otimes E_{2}\),

\[\eqalign{[e_{1}\bullet(f_{1}\odot v)](f_{0}^{\prime})&=e_{1}\bullet[(f_{1} \odot f_{2})\otimes e_{2}](f_{0}^{\prime})=e_{1}\bullet\langle f_{0}^{\prime}, f_{1}\odot f_{2}\rangle e_{2}\cr&=\langle f_{0}^{\prime},f_{1}\odot f_{2} \rangle(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})=[(f_{1}\odot f_{2})\otimes(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})](f _{0}^{\prime})\cr}\]

for \(f_{1}\in F_{1}\) and \(e_{1}\in E_{1}\). Hence

\[e_{1}\bullet(f_{1}\odot v)=(f_{1}\odot f_{2})\otimes(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\]

for \(f_{1}\otimes e_{1}\in F_{1}\otimes E_{1}\) and \(v:=f_{2}\otimes e_{2}\in F_{2}\otimes E_{2}\). By Proposition 1.5.2 there exists a unique hypocontinuous bilinear extension (1.5.17) of (1.5.15) satisfying

\[(f_{1}\otimes e_{1})\odot_{\bullet}v=e_{1}\bullet(f_{1}\odot v)\ ,\qquad f_{1} \otimes e_{1}\in F_{1}\otimes E_{1}\ ,\quad v\in F_{2}\stackrel{{ \sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{2}\ .\]

Thus (1.5.19) implies (1.5.18).

The results of this subsection are due to L. Schwartz. In fact, they are special cases of much more general theorems given in [Sch57b, chap. II] (also see [Sch57a]).

**General Hypothesis**

Throughout the remainder of this section we suppose that

\[\eqalign{&E\hbox{, $F$, and $E_{j}$, \ $j=0,1,2$, are Banach spaces and}\cr&E_{1}\times E_{2}\to E_{0}\ ,\quad(e_{1},e_{2})\mapsto e_{1}\bullet e_{2}\cr&i\hbox{$j=0$,\quad$(1,5.20)$}\cr&i\hbox{$j=1$,\quad$(1,5.20)$}\cr&i\hbox{$j=1$,\quad$(1,5.20)$}\cr&i\hbox{$j=0$,\quad$(1,5.20)$}\cr&i\hbox{$j=0$,\quad$(1,5.

---

### Point-Wise Multiplication

As a first application of the general extension result of Theorem 1.5.3 we define point-wise multiplication of a vector-valued smooth function with a vector-valued distribution and study some of its properties.

It is an immediate consequence of Leibniz' rule that for each \(m\in\bar{\mathbb{N}}\) point-wise multiplication induced by (1.5.20),

\[C^{m}(X,E_{1})\times C^{m}(X,E_{2})\to C^{m}(X,E_{0})\ ,\quad(a_{1},a_{2}) \mapsto a_{1}\bullet a_{2}\ ,\] (1.6.1)

is well-defined, bilinear and continuous.

Given \(a\in\mathcal{E}(X)\) and \(v\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X,E)\), we recall that \(av\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X,E)\) is defined by

\[av(\varphi):=v(a\varphi)\ ,\qquad\varphi\in\mathcal{D}(X)\ .\] (1.6.2)

It is easily verified that

\[(\varphi\mapsto a\varphi)\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{D}(X)\big{)}\ ,\qquad a \in\mathcal{E}(X)\ .\]

A Characterization of \(\mathcal{O}_{M}\)First we prove a characterization of \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\) that extends [1, (III.4.1.9)]. In addition, it explains the name 'space of multipliers' for \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\).

**1.6.1 Proposition**.: _Suppose that \(a\in\mathcal{E}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\). Then_

\[a\in\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\quad\text{iff}\quad(\varphi\mapsto \varphi a)\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n}),\mathcal{S}( \mathbb{R}^{n},E)\big{)}\ .\]

Proof.: Given \(a\in\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\) and \(k,m\in\mathbb{N}\), Leibniz' rule and (1.1.8) imply

\[q_{k,m}(\varphi a)\leq c\max_{|\alpha|\leq m}\sum_{\beta\leq\alpha}\sup_{x\in \mathbb{R}^{n}}(1+|x|^{2})^{k}\,|\partial^{\beta}\varphi(x)|\,|\partial^{ \alpha-\beta}a(x)|\leq cq_{\ell,m}(\varphi)\] (1.6.3)

for \(\varphi\in\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\), where \(\ell:=k+\max\{\,m_{\alpha-\beta}\ ;\ \beta\leq\alpha,\ |\alpha|\leq m\,\}\) and where \(m_{\alpha-\beta}\in\mathbb{N}\) are such that there exists \(c_{\alpha-\beta}\) satisfying \(|\partial^{\alpha-\beta}a(x)|\leq c_{\alpha-\beta}(1+|x|^{2})^{m_{\alpha-\beta }}\) for \(x\in\mathbb{R}^{n}\). This shows that

\[(\varphi\mapsto\varphi a)\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n}), \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\big{)}\ .\] (1.6.4)

Conversely, let (1.6.4) be true. Then, given \(\alpha\in\mathbb{N}\), there exist \(k,m\in\mathbb{N}\) and a positive constant \(c\) such that

\[\|\partial^{\alpha}(\varphi a)\|_{\infty}\leq q_{0,|\alpha|}(\varphi a)\leq cq _{k,m}(\varphi)\ ,\qquad\varphi\in\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\ .\]

---

Fix \(\psi\in{\cal D}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\) such that \(\psi\) equals \(1\) near zero. Since \(\tau_{x}\psi\in{\cal D}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\subset{\cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\) for \(x\in{\mathbb{R}}^{n}\), it follows that

\[|\partial^{\alpha}a(x)| =\big{|}\partial^{\alpha}\big{(}(\tau_{x}\psi)a\big{)}(x)\big{|} \leq cq_{k,m}(\tau_{x}\psi)\] \[\leq c\sup_{|\alpha|\leq m\atop|y\in{\mathbb{R}}^{n}}(1+|x-y|^{2}) ^{k}\,|\partial^{\alpha}\psi(y)|\leq c(1+|x|^{2})^{k}\] (1.6.5)

for \(x\in{\mathbb{R}}^{n}\), thanks to the trivial inequality \(1+|x-y|^{2}\leq 2(1+|x|^{2})(1+|y|^{2})\). Hence \(a\in{\cal O}_{M}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E)\).

#### 1.6.2 Corollary

_Suppose that \(a\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\). Then_

\[a\in{\cal O}_{M}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\quad\mbox{iff}\quad(u\mapsto au)\in{\cal L} \big{(}{\cal S}^{\prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\big{)}\ .\]

ProofFor simplicity, we put \({\cal O}_{M}={\cal O}_{M}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\) etc. If \(a\in{\cal O}_{M}\), it follows from Proposition 1.6.1 that \((\varphi\mapsto\varphi a)\in{\cal L}({\cal S})\). Hence the dual of this linear map, which is given by \(u\mapsto au\) for \(u\in{\cal S}^{\prime}\), satisfies \((u\mapsto au)\in{\cal L}({\cal S}^{\prime})\). Conversely, \((u\mapsto au)\in{\cal L}({\cal S}^{\prime})\) implies \((u\mapsto au)^{\prime}\in{\cal L}({\cal S})\) by the reflexivity of \({\cal S}\). Since the latter dual is the map \(\varphi\mapsto\varphi a\) for \(\varphi\in{\cal S}\), the assertion follows.

#### The General Theorem

Now it is easy to prove the following technical lemma that will be used in the proof of the next theorem, one of the main results of this subsection.

#### 1.6.3 Lemma

_Suppose that \(({\mathfrak{F}}_{1},{\mathfrak{F}}_{2};{\mathfrak{F}}_{0})\) is one of the triplets \(({\cal E},{\cal D}^{\prime};{\cal D}^{\prime})\), \(({\cal E},{\cal E}^{\prime};{\cal E}^{\prime})\), \(({\cal S},{\cal O}_{M};{\cal S})\), \(({\cal O}_{M},{\cal O}_{M};{\cal O}_{M})\), \(({\cal O}_{M},{\cal S}^{\prime};{\cal S}^{\prime})\), \(({\cal E},{\cal E};{\cal E})\), or \(({\cal E},{\cal D};{\cal D})\). Then 'point-wise multiplication'_

\[{\mathfrak{F}}_{1}(X)\times{\mathfrak{F}}_{2}(X,E)\to{\mathfrak{F}}_{0}(X,E)\ ,\quad(a,u)\mapsto au\] (1.6.6)

_is a well-defined hypocontinuous bilinear map._

ProofIt follows from (1.1.8) and (1.1.9) that \(B\) is a bounded subset of \({\cal O}_{M}({\mathbb{R}}^{n}\,,E)\) iff, given \(\alpha\in{\mathbb{N}}^{n}\), there exist \(m_{\alpha}\in{\mathbb{N}}\) and \(c_{\alpha}>0\) such that

\[|\partial^{\alpha}u(x)|\leq c_{\alpha}(1+|x|^{2})^{m_{\alpha}}\ ,\qquad x\in{ \mathbb{R}}^{n}\ ,\quad u\in B\ .\] (1.6.7)

Hence (1.6.3) shows that

\[(a\mapsto au)\in{\cal L}\big{(}{\cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n}),{\cal S}({\mathbb{R }}^{n},E)\big{)}\ ,\]

uniformly with respect to \(u\) in bounded subsets of \({\cal O}_{M}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E)\). Since the function defined by \(x\mapsto(1+|x|^{2})^{k}\partial^{\beta}\varphi(x)\) belongs to \({\cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\) for \(\varphi\in{\cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\), \(k\in{\mathbb{N}}\), and

---

\(\beta\in\mathbb{N}^{n}\), it follows from (1.6.3) that, given \(k,m\in\mathbb{N}\) and \(a\in\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\), there exists \(a_{k,\alpha}\in\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) such that

\[q_{k,m}(au)\leq c\max_{|\alpha|\leq k}\|a_{k,\alpha}\partial^{\alpha}u\|_{\infty }\ .\]

Hence

\[(u\mapsto au)\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E),\mathcal{S} (\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\big{)}\ ,\qquad a\in\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\ .\] (1.6.8)

Thus, letting \(M_{u}:=(a\mapsto au)\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n}),\mathcal{S }(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\big{)}\), we see from (1.6.8) that

\[(u\mapsto M_{u})\in\mathcal{L}\Big{(}\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E), \mathcal{L}_{s}\big{(}\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n}),\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n}, E)\big{)}\Big{)}\ .\]

Consequently, \(\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) being a Montel space, the Banach-Steinhaus theorem guarantees that

\[(u\mapsto M_{u})\in\mathcal{L}\Big{(}\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E), \mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n}),\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E) \big{)}\Big{)}\ ,\]

that is, the map \(u\mapsto au\) is continuous from \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\) into \(\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\), uniformly with respect to \(a\) in bounded subsets of \(\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\). This proves the assertion for the case \((\mathfrak{F}_{1},\mathfrak{F}_{2};\mathfrak{F}_{0})=(\mathcal{S},\mathcal{O} _{M};\mathcal{S})\).

Given \(a\in\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) and \(u\in\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\), it follows from Leibniz' rule that

\[\|\varphi\partial^{\alpha}(au)\|_{\infty}\leq c\Big{\|}\varphi\sum_{\beta\leq \alpha}\partial^{\beta}a\partial^{\alpha-\beta}u\Big{\|}_{\infty}\ ,\qquad \varphi\in\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\ .\]

Thus (1.6.7) implies the existence of \(m\in\mathbb{N}\) such that

\[\|\varphi\partial^{\alpha}(au)\|_{\infty}\leq c\sum_{\beta\leq\alpha}\|(1+|x|^ {2})^{m}\varphi\partial^{\beta}a\|_{\infty}\ ,\qquad u\in B\ .\]

This shows that \(a\mapsto au\) maps \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) continuously into \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\), uniformly with respect to \(u\) in bounded subsets of \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\). Similarly, we see that \(u\mapsto au\) maps \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\) continuously into itself, uniformly with respect to \(a\) in bounded subsets of \(\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\). This proves the assertion if \((\mathfrak{F}_{1},\mathfrak{F}_{2};\mathfrak{F}_{0})=(\mathcal{O}_{M}, \mathcal{O}_{M};\mathcal{O}_{M})\).

Since \(\operatorname{supp}(au)\subset\operatorname{supp}(a)\cap\operatorname{supp}(u)\) for \(a\in\mathcal{E}(X)\) and \(u\in\mathcal{D}(X,E)\), Leibniz' rule and the properties of LF-spaces easily imply that point-wise multiplication is separately continuous from \(\mathcal{E}(X)\times\mathcal{D}(X,E)\) into \(\mathcal{D}(X,E)\). Now hypocontinuity in the case \((\mathcal{E},\mathcal{D};\mathcal{D})\) follows from the fact that \(\mathcal{E}(X)\) and \(\mathcal{D}(X,E)\) are barreled.

If \((\mathfrak{F}_{1},\mathfrak{F}_{2};\mathfrak{F}_{0})=(\mathcal{E},\mathcal{E}; \mathcal{E})\), the assertion follows from (1.6.1). In all other cases Proposition 1.6.1 and Corollary 1.6.2 guarantee that the map (1.6.6) is well-defined, if this is not obvious anyhow. Moreover, in these cases

\[M_{a}:=(\varphi\mapsto a\varphi)\in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}_{0}^{\prime} (X),\mathfrak{F}_{2}^{\prime}(X)\big{)}\ ,\qquad a\in\mathfrak{F}_{1}(X)\ ,\]

and \(\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}_{j}^{\prime}(X),E\big{)}=\mathfrak{F}_{j}(X,E), \ j=0,2\), by reflexivity. Thus (1.6.6) is the linear map

\[\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}_{0}^{\prime}(X),\mathfrak{F}_{2}^{\prime}(X) \big{)}\times\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}_{2}^{\prime}(X),E\big{)}\to \mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}_{0}^{\prime}(X),E\big{)}\ ,\quad(a,u)\mapsto u\circ M_{a}\ ,\]

and the assertion follows from Lemma 1.1.1.

---

Now we can extend point-wise multiplication to the case that both factors are vector-valued.

**1.6.4 Theorem** _There exists a unique hypocontinuous bilinear map_

\[{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\to{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{0})\ ,\quad(a,u)\mapsto a\bullet u\ ,\]

_called_ **point-wise multiplication induced by** (1.5.20), _such that_

\[(\varphi\otimes e_{1})\bullet(\psi\otimes e_{2})=\varphi\psi\otimes(e_{1} \bullet e_{2})\]

_for \(a:=\varphi\otimes e_{1}\in{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{1}\) and \(u:=\psi\otimes e_{2}\in{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2}\). It restricts to a hypocontinuous bilinear map_

\[{\twelvenm F}_{1}(X,E_{1})\times{\twelvenm F}_{2}(X,E_{2})\to{\twelvenm F}_{0}(X, E_{0})\ ,\]

_where \(({\twelvenm F}_{1},{\twelvenm F}_{2};{\twelvenm F}_{0})\) is any one of the triplets \(({\cal E},{\cal E}^{\prime};{\cal E}^{\prime})\), \(({\cal S},{\cal O}_{M};{\cal S})\), \(({\cal O}_{M},{\cal O}_{M};{\cal O}_{M})\), \(({\cal O}_{M},{\cal S}^{\prime};{\cal S}^{\prime})\), \(({\cal E},{\cal E};{\cal E})\), or \(({\cal E},{\cal D};{\cal D})\)._

**Proof** Let \(({\twelvenm F}_{1},{\twelvenm F}_{2};{\twelvenm F}_{0})\) be as stated or \(({\twelvenm F}_{1},{\twelvenm F}_{2};{\twelvenm F}_{0})=({\cal E},{\cal D}^{ \prime};{\cal D}^{\prime})\), and write \(F_{j}\) for \({\twelvenm F}_{j}(X)\), \(j=0,1,2\). Then the spaces \(F_{j}\) are reflexive, complete, nuclear, and conuclear by Theorems 1.1.2 and 1.4.3. Moreover, \(F_{j}\mathrel{\widetilde{\otimes}}E_{j}={\twelvenm F}_{j}(X,E_{j}),\ j=0,1,2\), thanks to Theorem 1.4.9. Define the bilinear maps (1.5.14) and (1.5.15) by point-wise multiplication. It is easily verified that (1.5.16) is true and it follows from Lemma 1.6.3 that the map (1.5.15) is hypocontinuous. Hence Theorem 1.5.3 guarantees the existence of a unique hypocontinuous bilinear map

\[{\twelvenm F}_{1}(X,E_{1})\times{\twelvenm F}_{2}(X,E_{2})\to{\twelvenm F}_{0}( X,E_{0})\ ,\quad(a,u)\mapsto a\bullet u\]

satisfying (1.6.10) for \(a:=\varphi\otimes e_{1}\in{\twelvenm F}_{1}(X)\otimes E_{1}\) and \(u:=v\otimes e_{2}\in{\twelvenm F}_{2}(X)\otimes E_{2}\). The assertion is now an obvious consequence of the almost trivial fact that the separately continuous bilinear map (1.6.11) is uniquely determined by its restriction to the subspace \(\bigl{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{1}\bigr{)}\times\bigl{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2 }\bigr{)}\) that is dense by Theorem 1.3.6.

**Basic Properties of Multiplications**

**1.6.5 Remarks** (a): Since \(E_{2}\times E_{1}\to E_{0}\), \((e_{2},e_{1})\mapsto e_{1}\bullet e_{2}\) is a multiplication as well, the assertions of Theorem 1.6.4 are 'symmetric' with respect to \(E_{1}\) and \(E_{2}\), that is, the roles of \(E_{1}\) and \(E_{2}\) can be interchanged. This fact will often be employed in the following, usually without further mention.
**(b):** Point-wise multiplication induced by (1.5.20), as defined in Theorem 1.6.4, coincides on regular distributions with point-wise multiplication in the usual sense. In other words, if \(a\in{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\) and \(u\in L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{2})\) then \(a\bullet u\in L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{0})\) and

\[a\bullet u(\cdot)=a(\cdot)\bullet u(\cdot)\ .\]

Observe that this justifies the use of the name 'point-wise multiplication' for the bilinear map of Theorem 1.6.4.

---

ProofSince \(L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{2})\hookrightarrow{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\), it follows from Theorem 1.6.4 and an obvious estimate that both sides of (1.6.12) are separately continuous bilinear maps

\[{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\times L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{2})\to{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{0})\ .\]

Theorem 1.3.6(viii) immediately implies

\[{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2}\stackrel{{ d}}{{\hookrightarrow}}L_{1,{ \rm loc}}(X,E_{2})\ .\]

Thus we deduce from (1.6.10) that both sides of (1.6.12) coincide on the dense subspace \(\bigl{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{1}\bigr{)}\times\bigl{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2} \bigr{)}\) of \({\cal E}(X,E_{1})\times L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{2})\). Hence the assertion follows.

**(c) Leibniz' rule** is valid in the general case as well. More precisely, if \(p\) is a polynomial in \(n\) indeterminates then

\[p(\partial)(a\bullet u)=\sum_{\beta}{1\over\beta!}(\partial^{\beta}a)\bullet p ^{(\beta)}(\partial)u\]

for \(a\in{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\) and \(u\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\), where \(p^{(\beta)}:=\partial^{\beta}p\). In particular:

\[\partial^{\alpha}(a\bullet u)=\sum_{\beta\leq\alpha}{\alpha\choose\beta}( \partial^{\beta}a)\bullet\partial^{\alpha-\beta}u\ ,\qquad a\in{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\ , \quad u\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\ .\]

ProofIt follows from \(\partial^{\alpha}\in{\cal L}\bigl{(}{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\bigr{)}\) and \(p^{(\beta)}(\partial)\in{\cal L}\bigl{(}{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\bigr{)}\) that both sides of (1.6.14) define separately continuous bilinear maps:

\[{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\to{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{0})\ .\]

Thanks to Lemma 1.3.2 and to property (1.6.10) they coincide on the linear subspace \(\bigl{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{1}\bigr{)}\times\bigl{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2}\bigr{)}\). Since, by Theorem 1.3.6(ii) and (v), this subspace is dense in \({\cal E}(X,E_{1})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\), they coincide everywhere.

**(d)**: If \((a,u)\in{\cal E}(X,E_{1})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{2})\) then

\[{\rm supp}(a\bullet u)\subset{\rm supp}(a)\cap{\rm supp}(u)\ .\]

ProofLet \(K:={\rm supp}(a)\) and denote by \(K_{\varepsilon}:=\bigl{\{}\,x\in X\ ;\ {\rm dist}(x,K)<\varepsilon\,\bigr{\}}\) the open \(\varepsilon\)-neighborhood of \(K\) in \(X\) for \(\varepsilon>0\). Choose \(\psi_{\varepsilon}\in{\cal E}(X)\) with \({\rm supp}(\psi_{\varepsilon})\subset K_{\varepsilon}\) and \(\psi|\,K=1\). Since \({\cal E}(X)\otimes E_{1}\) is dense in \({\cal E}(X,E_{1})\), there exists a sequence \((a_{j})\) in \({\cal E}(X)\otimes E_{1}\) converging in \({\cal E}(X,E_{1})\) towards \(a\). Then \(b_{j}:=\psi_{\varepsilon}\,a_{j}\in{\cal E}(X)\otimes E_{1}\) and \({\rm supp}(b_{j})\subset K_{\varepsilon}\). It is easily verified that \({\rm supp}(b_{j}\bullet u)\subset\overline{K}_{\varepsilon}\cap{\rm supp}(u)=: M_{\varepsilon}\) and that

\[{\cal D}^{\prime}_{M_{\varepsilon}}(X,E_{0}):=\bigl{\{}\,v\in{\cal D}^{\prime} (X,E_{0})\ ;\ {\rm supp}(v)\subset M_{\varepsilon}\,\bigr{\}}\]

is a closed linear subspace of \({\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{0})\). Now we deduce from Theorem 1.6.4 that \(b_{j}\bullet u\to a\bullet u\) in \({\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E_{0})\), hence in \({\cal D}^{\prime}_{M_{\varepsilon}}(X,E_{0})\). Consequently, \({\rm supp}(a\bullet u)\subset M_{\varepsilon}\) for each \(\varepsilon>0\), which implies the assertion.

---

**(e)**: Let \(E_{3}\), \(E_{4}\), and \(E_{5}\) be further Banach spaces and suppose that there are multiplications

all denoted by \(\bullet\) , that are associative, that is,

\[(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\bullet e_{3}=e_{1}\bullet(e_{2}\bullet e_{3})\ ,\qquad e_{j} \in E_{j}\ ,\quad j=1,2,3\ .\] (1.6.16)

Then point-wise multiplication is associative as well, when defined, that is,

\[(u_{1}\bullet u_{2})\bullet u_{3}=u_{1}\bullet(u_{2}\bullet u_{3})\ ,\qquad u_{j} \in\mathfrak{F}_{j}(X,E_{j})\ ,\quad j=1,2,3\ ,\] (1.6.17)

where \((\mathfrak{F}_{1},\mathfrak{F}_{2},\mathfrak{F}_{3})=\big{\{}(\mathcal{E}, \mathcal{E},\mathcal{D}^{\prime}),(\mathcal{O}_{M},\mathcal{O}_{M},\mathcal{S} ^{\prime})\big{\}}\).

**Proof** : It follows from Theorem 1.6.4 that both sides of (1.6.17) define separately continuous trilinear maps

\[\prod_{j=1}^{3}\mathfrak{F}_{j}(X,E_{j})\to\mathfrak{F}_{3}(X,E_{5})\]

that coincide on the dense linear subspace \(\prod_{j=1}^{3}\mathcal{D}(X)\otimes E_{j}\), hence everywhere.
**(f)**: Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E},\mathcal{S},\mathcal{O}_{M}, \mathcal{D}^{\prime},\mathcal{E}^{\prime},\mathcal{S}^{\prime}\}\). Then the map

\[E_{1}\times\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\to\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{0})\ ,\quad(e_{1},u) \mapsto e_{1}\bullet u:=(1\otimes e_{1})\bullet u\] (1.6.18)

is bilinear and continuous, and

\[\partial^{\alpha}(e_{1}\bullet u)=e_{1}\bullet\partial^{\alpha}u\ ,\qquad \alpha\in\mathbb{N}^{n}\ ,\quad e_{1}\in E_{1}\ ,\quad u\in\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\ .\] (1.6.19)

**Proof** : Since \(1\otimes e_{1}\in\mathcal{O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E_{1})\hookrightarrow\mathcal{ E}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E_{1})\), it follows from Theorem 1.6.4 and Remark (a) that (1.6.18) is a well-defined separately continuous bilinear map. Moreover, given \(u=v\otimes e_{2}\in\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E_{2}\) and \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\),

\[(e_{1}\bullet u)(\varphi) =\big{[}(1\otimes e_{1})\bullet(v\otimes e_{2})\big{]}(\varphi)= \langle v,\varphi\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}}e_{1}\bullet e_{2}=e_{1} \bullet\big{(}\langle v,\varphi\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}}e_{2}\big{)}\] \[=e_{1}\bullet u(\varphi)\ .\]

Thus the density of \(\mathfrak{F}(X)\otimes E_{2}\) in \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\) implies

\[(e_{1}\bullet u)(\varphi)=e_{1}\bullet u(\varphi)\ ,\qquad e_{1}\in E_{1}\ , \quad u\in\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\ ,\quad\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\ .\] (1.6.20)

Consequently, given a bounded subset \(B\) of \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\),

\[\sup_{\varphi\in B}|(e_{1}\bullet u)(\varphi)|_{E_{0}}\leq|e_{1}|_{E_{1}}\sup_ {\varphi\in B}|u(\varphi)|_{E_{2}}\ ,\qquad e_{1}\in E_{1}\ ,\quad u\in \mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\ .\]

This proves the continuity of (1.6.18), thanks to Theorem 1.4.9. Lastly, (1.6.19) is a consequence of (c).

---

**(g)**: Let \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S},{\cal O}_{M},{\cal D}^{\prime},{\cal E} ^{\prime},{\cal S}^{\prime}\}\) and consider the multiplication

\[{\cal L}(E,F)\times E\to F\ ,\quad(T,e)\mapsto T\bullet e:=Te\ .\] (1.6.21)

Then it follows from (f) that (1.6.21) induces a continuous bilinear map

\[{\cal L}(E,F)\times\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\to\mathfrak{F}(X,F)\ ,\quad(T,u)\mapsto T \bullet u:=Tu\ .\]

In particular, each \(T\in{\cal L}(E,F)\) induces a continuous linear map via (1.6.21),

\[(u\mapsto T\bullet u)\in{\cal L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}(X,E),\mathfrak{F}(X,F) \big{)}\ .\] (1.6.22)

We denote it by \(T\) as well and call it the linear map **induced by \(T\in{\cal L}(E,F)\) via point-wise multiplication**. Moreover, (1.6.19) implies \(\partial^{\alpha}\circ T=T\circ\partial^{\alpha}\) for \(\alpha\in\mathbb{N}^{n}\), that is, the diagram

is commutative for \(\alpha\in\mathbb{N}^{n}\). If \(T\in{\cal L}(E,F)\) is injective, then (1.6.22) is injective as well. Consequently,

\[i:\,E\hookrightarrow F\quad\mbox{implies}\quad i:\,\mathfrak{F}(X,E) \hookrightarrow\mathfrak{F}(X,F)\ .\]

**Proof** We have to prove only the injectivity assertion. Thus suppose that \(Tu=0\) for some \(u\in\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) and that \(T\in{\cal L}(E,F)\) is injective. Then we obtain from (1.6.20) that \(T\big{(}u(\varphi)\big{)}=0\) for each \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\). Hence \(u(\varphi)=0\) for each \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\), that is, \(u=0\).

**(h)**: Suppose that \(E_{1}=E_{2}=:E\) and multiplication (1.5.20) is symmetric, that is, \(e_{1}\bullet e_{2}=e_{2}\bullet e_{1}\) for \(e_{j}\in E\). Then \(a\bullet u=u\bullet a\) for \(a\in{\cal E}(X,E)\) and \(u\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E)\).

**Proof** This is an immediate consequence of (b), the density of \({\cal D}(X,E)\times{\cal D}(X,E)\) in \({\cal E}(X,E)\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X,E)\), and the separate continuity of point-wise multiplication.

**1.6.6 Corollary**: _Suppose that \((E,\bullet)\) is a \([\)commutative\(]\) Banach algebra and that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S},{\cal O}_{M}\}\). Then \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\) is a locally convex \([\)commutative\(]\) algebra with respect to point-wise multiplication, a_ **multiplication algebra**_. Multiplication is continuous if \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S}\}\), and hypocontinuous if \(\mathfrak{F}={\cal O}_{M}\). If \(E\) possesses a unit, \(e_{0}\), then \({\cal E}(X,E)\) and \({\cal O}_{M}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\) possess a unit as well, namely \(1\otimes e_{0}\)._

**Proof** This follows from Theorem 1.6.4, Remarks 1.6.5(e) and (h), appropriate continuous injections given in Theorem 1.3.6, and the fact that hypocontinuous maps are continuous on barreled spaces.

---

### Scalar Products and Duality Pairings

In this subsection we show, in particular, that, given \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S}\}\), there exists a unique hypocontinuous bilinear map

\[\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X,E^{\prime})\times\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\to\mathbb{K}\] (1.7.1)

that extends in a natural way the duality pairing \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\times\mathfrak{F}(X)\to\mathbb{K}\). In fact, we consider more general situations that will be needed in the remaining subsections.

**1.7.1 Lemma**: _Let \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S},{\cal D}^{\prime},{\cal E}^{\prime },{\cal S}^{\prime}\}\). Then the bilinear map_

\[\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\times\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\to E\ ,\quad(u,\varphi)\mapsto u (\varphi)\] (1.7.2)

_is hypocontinuous._

**Proof** Since \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime\prime}=\mathfrak{F}\), it follows from Theorem 1.4.9 that \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)={\cal L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X),E\big{)}\). Hence the map (1.7.2) is well-defined and continuous in \(u\), uniformly on bounded subsets of \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\). Thanks to the fact that \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\) is barreled, bounded subsets of \({\cal L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X),E\big{)}\) are equicontinuous by the uniform boundedness principle. Thus (1.7.2) is continuous in \(\varphi\), uniformly with respect to \(u\) varying in bounded subsets of \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\).

It is easy to prove the following general existence theorem that will imply, in particular, the desired extension (1.7.1).

**1.7.2 Theorem**: _Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S},{\cal D}^{\prime},{\cal E}^{\prime },{\cal S}^{\prime}\}\). Then there exists a unique hypocontinuous bilinear map_

\[\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X,E_{1})\times\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\to E_{0}\ ,\quad(u^{ \prime},u)\mapsto\langle u^{\prime}\bullet u\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}}\ ,\] (1.7.3)

_the_ **scalar product induced by multiplication**__(1.5.20), _such that_

\[\big{\langle}(\varphi\otimes e_{1})\bullet(\psi\otimes e_{2})\big{\rangle}_{ \mathfrak{F}}=\langle\varphi,\psi\rangle_{\cal D}(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\] (1.7.4)

_for \(\varphi,\psi\in{\cal D}(X)\) and \(e_{j}\in E_{j}\), \(j=1,2\)._

**Proof** Put \(F_{0}:=\mathbb{K}\), \(F_{1}:=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X)\), and \(F_{2}:=\mathfrak{F}(X)\). Then the \(F_{j}\) are reflexive, complete, nuclear, and conuclear LCSs. Consequently, Theorem 1.4.9 guarantees that \(F_{2}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{2}=\mathfrak{F}(X,E_{2})\), and it is trivially true that \(F_{0}\otimes E_{0}=F_{0}\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}E_{0}=E_{0}\). Define the bilinear maps (1.5.14) and (1.5.15) by \(f_{1}\odot f_{2}:=\langle f_{1},f_{2}\rangle_{F_{2}}\) and \(f_{1}\mathbin{\mathchoice{\vbox{\hbox{\raise 0.43pt\hbox{$\circ$}}}}{\vbox{\hbox{ \raise 0.43pt\hbox{$\circ$}}}}{\vbox{\hbox{\raise 0.43pt\hbox{$\circ$}}}}{\vbox{ \hbox{\raise 0.43pt\hbox{$\circ$}}}}{\vbox{\hbox{\raise 0.43pt\hbox{$ \circ$}}}}}v:=v(f_{1})\), respectively. Then Lemma 1.7.1 shows that (1.5.15) is hypocontinuous. Since it is obvious that condition (1.5.16) is satisfied, Theorem 1.5.3 gives the assertion.

**1.7.3 Remark** Suppose that \(u\in L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{1})\) and \(v\in{\cal D}(X,E_{2})\). Then

\[\langle u\bullet v\rangle_{\cal D}=\int_{X}u(x)\bullet v(x)\,dx\ .\] (1.7.5)

---

**Proof** Since \(L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{1})\stackrel{{ d}}{{\hookrightarrow}}{\cal D}^{ \prime}(X,E_{1})\), Theorem 1.7.2 implies that the map

\[L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{1})\times{\cal D}(X,E_{2})\to E_{0}\ ,\quad(u,v)\mapsto \langle u\bullet v\rangle_{\cal D}\] (1.7.6)

is bilinear and separately continuous. From (1.6.13) and Theorem 1.3.6 we infer that

\[\big{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{1}\big{)}\times\big{(}{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2} \big{)}\stackrel{{ d}}{{\subset}}L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E_{1})\times{ \cal D}(X,E_{2})\ .\] (1.7.7)

It is obvious that (1.7.5) is true for \(u\in{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{1}\) and \(v\in{\cal D}(X)\otimes E_{2}\). Hence the assertion follows from (1.7.7) and the separate continuity of the map (1.7.6).

**Parseval's Formula**

As a first application of Theorem 1.7.2 we obtain a natural extension of Parseval's formula for the Fourier transform.

**1.7.4 Proposition** _Parseval's formula is valid for vector-valued distributions, that is,_

\[\langle u\bullet\varphi\rangle_{\cal S}=(2\pi)^{-n}\langle\widehat{u}\bullet \stackrel{{\chi}}{{\not\!\partial}}\rangle_{\cal S}\ ,\qquad u\in{\cal S}^{ \prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E_{1})\ ,\quad\varphi\in{\cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E_{2})\ .\] (1.7.8)

**Proof** Thanks to Theorem 1.7.2 and the fact that the Fourier transform and reflection are toplinear automorphisms, it follows that both sides of (1.7.8) are separately continuous bilinear maps from \({\cal S}^{\prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E_{1})\times{\cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E_{2})\) into \(E_{0}\). By (1.7.4) and the well-known Parseval formula for scalar distributions the two expressions on either side of (1.7.8) coincide on the dense linear subspace

\[\big{(}{\cal S}^{\prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\otimes E_{1}\big{)}\times\big{(}{ \cal S}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\otimes E_{2}\big{)}\ .\]

Hence they are equal.

**Duality Pairings**

By specializing the above results to the case where (1.5.20) is a duality pairing we obtain the desired map (1.7.1).

**1.7.5 Theorem** _Let \(E\) be a Banach space and let \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S}\}\). Then there exists a unique hypocontinuous bilinear map_

\[\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X,E^{\prime})\times\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\to{\mathbb{K}}\ , \quad(u^{\prime},u)\mapsto\langle u^{\prime},u\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}(X,E)}\ ,\]

_the_ **duality pairing between \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X,E^{\prime})\) and \(\mathfrak{F}(X,E)\)**, _such that_

\[\langle u^{\prime},u\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}(X,E)}=\int_{X}\bigl{\langle}u^{ \prime}(x),u(x)\bigr{\rangle}_{E}\,dx\] (1.7.9)

_for \(u^{\prime}\in{\cal D}(X,E^{\prime})\) and \(u\in{\cal D}(X,E)\)._

---

**Proof** Let \(E_{1}:=E^{\prime}\), \(E_{2}:=E\), and \(E_{0}:=\mathbb{K}\), and put \(e_{1}\bullet e_{2}:=\langle e_{1},e_{2}\rangle_{E}\). Then the assertion follows from Theorem 1.7.2 and Remark 1.7.3.

**1.7.6 Remarks**: **(a)** It is also true that

\[\langle u^{\prime},u\rangle_{{\cal D}(X,E)}=\int_{X}\bigl{\langle}u^{\prime}(x ),u(x)\bigr{\rangle}_{E}\,dx\ ,\qquad(u^{\prime},u)\in L_{1,{\rm loc}}(X,E^{ \prime})\times{\cal D}(X,E)\ ,\]

and

\[\langle u^{\prime},u\rangle_{{\cal S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)}=\int_{\mathbb{R}^{n}} \bigl{\langle}u^{\prime}(x),u(x)\bigr{\rangle}_{E}\,dx\ ,\qquad(u^{\prime},u)\in L _{p}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E^{\prime})\times{\cal S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\ ,\]

where \(1\leq p<\infty\).

**Proof** The first part of the assertion is a consequence of Remark 1.7.3. The second one follows from

\[{\cal D}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E^{\prime})\stackrel{{ d}}{{\hookrightarrow }}L_{p}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E^{\prime})\stackrel{{ d}}{{\hookrightarrow }}{\cal S}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E^{\prime})\ ,\qquad 1\leq p<\infty\ ,\]

from \({\cal D}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\stackrel{{ d}}{{\hookrightarrow}}{ \cal S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\), and from the separate continuity of the bilinear map

\[(u^{\prime},u)\mapsto\int_{\mathbb{R}^{n}}\bigl{\langle}u^{\prime}(x),u(x) \bigr{\rangle}_{E}\,dx\]

on \(L_{p}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E^{\prime})\times{\cal S}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\).

**(b)** Theorem 1.7.5 contains a more precise description of the duality pairing of Corollary 1.4.10.

### Tensor Products of Distributions and Kernel Theorems

It is the purpose of this subsection to define tensor products of arbitrary vector-valued distributions. These results are of interest for their own sake. In addition, they will be the basis for an important extension of convolutions of vector-valued distributions given in the next section.

**Approximation by Tensor Products**

**1.8.1 Theorem**: _Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal D},{\cal E},{\cal S},{\cal D}^{\prime},{\cal E}^{ \prime},{\cal S}^{\prime}\}\) and \(X_{j}\subset\mathbb{R}^{n_{j}}\), \(j=1,2\), are open. Then \({\cal D}(X_{1})\otimes{\cal D}(X_{2},E)\) is sequentially dense in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\)._

**Proof** Let \(\varphi\in{\cal D}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) be given and put \(K_{j}:={\rm pr}_{j}\bigl{(}{\rm supp}(\varphi)\bigr{)}\), where

\[{\rm pr}_{j}:\,\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}\times\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}}\to\mathbb{R}^{n_{j}} \ ,\qquad j=1,2\ ,\]

are the canonical projections. Then \(K_{j}\subset\subset X_{j}\) and there exist \(\psi_{j}\in{\cal D}(X_{j})\) with \(\psi_{j}\,|\,K_{j}=1\). It follows that \(\psi_{1}\otimes\psi_{2}\in{\cal D}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\) and \(\psi_{1}\otimes\psi_{2}\,|\,{\rm supp}(\varphi)=1\).

---

Thanks to Lemma 1.3.7 there exists a sequence \((p_{k})\) of polynomials on \(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}\times\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}}\) with coefficients in \(E\), converging in \(\mathcal{E}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) towards \(\varphi\). Then the sequence \(\big{(}(\psi_{1}\otimes\psi_{2})p_{k}\big{)}_{k\in\mathbb{N}}\) lies in \(\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\otimes\mathcal{D}(X_{2},E)\) and converges in \(\mathcal{E}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) towards \(\varphi\). Since the supports of \((\psi_{1}\otimes\psi_{2})p_{k}\) are contained in a fixed compact set, the convergence takes place in \(\mathcal{D}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\). It is clear that

\[\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\otimes\mathcal{D}(X_{2},E)\subset\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}) \otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\subset\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\ .\] (1.8.1)

Since \(\mathcal{D}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) is sequentially dense in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) by [1, Corollary V.2.4.2] and Remark 1.3.4, the assertion follows from (1.8.1) and what has already been proven, provided \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E},\mathcal{F}\}\). If \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D}^{\prime},\mathcal{E}^{\prime},\mathcal{F}^{\prime}\}\), we obtain from the already proven facts and Proposition 1.3.3 that

\[\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\otimes\mathcal{D}(X_{2},E)\stackrel{{ d}}{{ \subset}}\mathcal{D}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\stackrel{{ d}}{{ \subset}}\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\]

with sequential density.

**1.8.2 Corollary**: _If \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E},\mathcal{S},\mathcal{D}^{\prime}, \mathcal{E}^{\prime},\mathcal{S}^{\prime}\}\) then \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\) is sequentially dense in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\)._

**Proof** This is now obvious from \(\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\otimes\mathcal{D}(X_{2},E)\subset\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}) \otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\) and from observation (1.3.16).

### Tensor Products of Distributions

As a preparation for defining tensor products of distributions we establish the following technical result.

**1.8.3 Lemma**: _Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E}\}\). If \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\) and \(u_{1}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1},E)\) then_

\[\big{[}x_{2}\mapsto u_{1}\big{(}\varphi(\cdot,x_{2})\big{)}\big{]}\in \mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\]

_and_

\[\partial^{\alpha}u_{1}\big{(}\varphi(\cdot,x_{2})\big{)}=u_{1}\big{(}\partial _{2}^{\alpha}\varphi(\cdot,x_{2})\big{)}\ ,\qquad\alpha\in\mathbb{N}^{n_{2}}\ .\]

**Proof** If \(\varphi\in\mathcal{D}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\), let \(K_{j}:=\operatorname{pr}_{j}\bigl{(}\operatorname{supp}(\varphi)\bigr{)}\). Then \(\operatorname{supp}(\varphi)\subset K_{1}\times K_{2}\) and \(K_{j}\subset\subset X_{j}\). From this it follows easily that

\[\big{[}x_{2}\mapsto\varphi(\cdot,x_{2})\big{]}\in\mathfrak{F}\bigl{(}X_{2}, \mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\bigr{)}\ .\]

Now, using \(u_{1}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1},E)=\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}), E\big{)}\), it is not difficult to derive the asserted properties.

---

Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E}\}\) and let \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\) and \(u_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\) be given. Then we put

\[u_{1}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}:=\big{[}x_{2}\mapsto u_{1}\big{(} \varphi(\cdot,x_{2})\big{)}\big{]}\] (1.8.2)

and

\[u_{2}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}:=\big{[}x_{1}\mapsto u_{2}\big{(} \varphi(x_{1},\cdot)\big{)}\big{]}\ .\] (1.8.3)

In other words, the **symbolic notation**\(u_{j}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\) means that the distribution \(u_{j}\) acts on the function following it as a function of the variable \(x_{j}\), the other variable being a free parameter.

It follows from Lemma 1.8.3 and Theorem 1.7.2 that, given \(u_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\), \(j=1,2\), and \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\),

\[\big{\langle}u_{1}\bullet u_{2}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle} _{\mathfrak{F}}\ ,\quad\big{\langle}u_{2}\bullet u_{1}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2}) \big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}\] (1.8.4)

are well-defined elements of \(E_{0}\).

Now we are prepared for the proof of the main result of this subsection.

1.8.4 Theorem: _Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E}\}\). Given \(u_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\), \(j=1,2\), there exists a unique distribution \(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E_{0})\), the_ **tensor product of \(u_{1}\) and \(u_{2}\) with respect to the multiplication** (1.5.20), _satisfying_

\[u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=u_{1}(\varphi_{1}) \bullet u_{2}(\varphi_{2})\ ,\qquad\varphi_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})\ ,\] (1.8.5)

_such that the map_

\[\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1},E_{1})\times\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{2},E_{2}) \to\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E_{0})\ ,\quad(u_{1},u_{2}) \mapsto u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}\] (1.8.6)

_is bilinear and hypocontinuous. It can be evaluated by_ **Fubini's rule**_:_

\[u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(\varphi)=\big{\langle}u_{1}\bullet u_{2}\big{(} \varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}=\big{\langle}u_{1} \big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\bullet u_{2}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}^{ \prime}}\] (1.8.7)

_for \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\)._

**Proof** Put \(X_{0}:=X_{1}\times X_{2}\) and \(F_{j}:=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j})\), \(j=0,1,2\). Then the \(F_{j}\) satisfy the hypotheses of Theorem 1.5.3 and \(F_{j}\mathaccent 869{\otimes}E_{j}=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\), \(j=0,1,2\), by Theorem 1.4.9. Define the maps (1.5.14) and (1.5.15) by

\[\varphi\mapsto f_{1}\odot f_{2}(\varphi):=\big{\langle}f_{1},f_{2}\big{(} \varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}\]

and

\[\varphi\mapsto f_{1}\mathaccent 869{\otimes}v(\varphi)\ :=v\big{(}f_{1}\big{(} \varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{)}\]

for \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{0})\), respectively. It follows from Lemma 1.8.3 that they are well-defined. From that lemma we also infer that

\[T_{f_{1}}:=\big{[}\varphi\mapsto f_{1}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},\cdot)\big{)}\big{]} \in\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}(X_{0}),\mathfrak{F}(X_{2})\big{)}\ .\] (1.8.8)

---

Thus, since \(f_{1}\odot v=v\circ T_{f_{1}}\), we obtain from Lemma 1.1.1 that the map (1.5.15) is hypocontinuous. Given \(f_{j}\in F_{j},\ \varphi_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{j}),\ j=1,2\), and \(e_{2}\in E_{2}\), it is clear that

\[[f_{1}\odot(f_{2}\otimes e_{2})](\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=\langle f_{1}, \varphi_{1}\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}}\langle f_{2},\varphi_{2}\rangle_{\mathfrak{F }}e_{2}=[(f_{1}\odot f_{2})\otimes e_{2}](\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})\ .\]

Since \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2})\) is dense in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{0})\) by Corollary 1.8.2, we infer that condition (1.5.16) is satisfied. Now the first part of the assertion follows from Theorem 1.5.3.

From Lemma 1.8.3 we deduce that

\[[\varphi\mapsto u_{j}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}]\in\mathcal{L}\big{(} \mathfrak{F}(X_{0}),\mathfrak{F}(X_{3-j},E_{3-j})\big{)}\ ,\ \ \ \ \ u_{j}\in \mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\ ,\ \ j=1,2\ .\]

Hence, given \(\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{0})\), Theorem 1.7.2 guarantees the existence of hypocontinuous scalar products \(\big{\langle}u_{1}\bullet u_{2}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle} _{\mathfrak{F}}\) and \(\big{\langle}u_{1}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\bullet u_{2}\big{\rangle} _{\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}}\) satisfying

\[\big{\langle}(f_{1}\otimes e_{1})\bullet(f_{2}\otimes e_{2})\big{(}\varphi(x_{ 1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}=\big{\langle}f_{1},f_{2}\big{(} \varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\]

and

\[\big{\langle}(f_{1}\otimes e_{1})\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\bullet(f_{ 2}\otimes e_{2})\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}}=\big{\langle}f_{1}\big{(} \varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)},f_{2}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}}(e_{1} \bullet e_{2})\]

for \(u_{j}:=f_{j}\otimes e_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j})\otimes E_{j},\ \ j=1,2\), respectively. Choosing \(\varphi:=\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2}\) in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2})\), we see that

\[\begin{split}\big{\langle}u_{1}\bullet u_{2}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1} ,x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}&=\big{\langle}u_{1} \big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\bullet u_{2}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}^{ \prime}}\\ &=\langle f_{1},\varphi_{1}\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}}\langle f_{2}, \varphi_{2}\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}}(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\\ &=\big{(}\langle f_{1},\varphi_{1}\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}}e_{1} \big{)}\bullet\big{(}\langle f_{2},\varphi_{2}\rangle_{\mathfrak{F}}e_{2} \big{)}\\ &=u_{1}(\varphi_{1})\bullet u_{2}(\varphi_{2})=u_{1}\otimes_{ \bullet}u_{2}(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})\ .\end{split}\] (1.8.9)

From \(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{0},E_{0})\), from (1.8.8), and from Theorem 1.7.2 we infer that each one of the trilinear maps

\[\mathfrak{F}(X_{0})\times\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1},E_{1})\times\mathfrak{F} ^{\prime}(X_{2},E_{2})\to E_{0}\]

sending \((\varphi,u_{1},u_{2})\)

\[\text{to }u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(\varphi)\ ,\quad\text{to }\big{\langle}u_{1} \bullet u_{2}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\big{\rangle}_{\mathfrak{F}}\ ,\quad\text{or to }\big{\langle}u_{1}\big{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\big{)}\bullet u_{2}\big{\rangle}_{ \mathfrak{F}^{\prime}}\ ,\]

respectively, is separately continuous. By (1.8.9) they are all equal on the linear subspace

\[\big{(}\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2})\big{)}\times\big{(} \mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\otimes E_{2}\big{)}\times\big{(}\mathfrak{F}^{ \prime}(X_{2})\otimes E_{2}\big{)}\ ,\]

which is dense by Theorem 1.3.6 and Corollary 1.8.2. Hence they are all equal, that is, Fubini's rule is valid.

---

**Basic Properties**

**1.8.5 Remarks**:
**(a)**: If \(u_{j}\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j}),\;\;j=1,2,\) then

\[\mbox{supp}(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2})\subset\mbox{supp}(u_{1})\times\mbox{ supp}(u_{2})\]

with equality, provided \(e_{1}\bullet e_{2}\neq 0\) whenever \(e_{j}\in\mbox{\Large$\stackrel{{\mbox{\large$\sharp$}}}{{E_{j}}}$}.\)

**Proof** Let \(A_{j}:=\mbox{supp}(u_{j}).\) If \(\mbox{supp}(\varphi)\subset{\mathbb{R}}^{n}\times A_{2}^{\varepsilon}\) then

\[u_{2}\bigl{(}\varphi(x_{1},x_{2})\bigr{)}=0\ ,\qquad x_{1}\in X_{1}\ ,\]

hence \(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(\varphi)=0\) by Fubini's rule. Similarly, we see that \(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(\varphi)=0\) if \(\mbox{supp}(\varphi)\subset A_{1}^{\varepsilon}\times{\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\). Consequently, \(\mbox{supp}(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2})\subset A_{1}\times A_{2}.\) On the other hand, given \((x_{1},x_{2})\in A_{1}\times A_{2}\) and any product neighborhood \(U_{1}\times U_{2}\) of \((x_{1},x_{2})\) in \(X_{1}\times X_{2}\), there exist \(\varphi_{j}\in{\cal D}(U_{j})\) such that \(u_{j}(\varphi_{j})\neq 0.\) Hence

\[u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=u_{1}(\varphi_{1}) \bullet u_{2}(\varphi_{2})\neq 0\]

if \(e_{1}\bullet e_{2}\neq 0\) for \(e_{j}\in\mbox{\Large$\stackrel{{\mbox{\large$\sharp$}}}{{E_{j}}}$}.\)
**(b)**: Given \(u_{j}\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\),

\[\partial_{1}^{\alpha_{1}}\partial_{2}^{\alpha_{2}}(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2} )=(\partial_{1}^{\alpha_{1}}u_{1})\otimes_{\bullet}(\partial_{2}^{\alpha_{2}}u _{2})\ ,\qquad\alpha_{j}\in{\mathbb{N}}^{n_{j}}\ .\] (1.8.10)

**Proof** It follows from Theorem 1.8.4 and the continuity properties of the derivative that both sides of (1.8.10) define separately continuous bilinear maps from \({\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1},E_{1})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{2},E_{2})\) into \({\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E_{0}).\) From (1.8.5) it is obvious that they coincide on the dense linear subspace \(\bigl{(}{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1})\otimes E_{1}\bigr{)}\times\bigl{(}{\cal D}^{ \prime}(X_{2})\otimes E_{2}\bigr{)}\), hence everywhere.
**(c)**: Let the associativity hypotheses of Remark 1.6.5(e) be satisfied and let \(X_{3}\) be a nonempty open subset of \({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{3}}\). Then

\[(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2})\otimes_{\bullet}u_{3}=u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}(u_ {2}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{3})\ ,\qquad u_{j}\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\ ,\quad j =1,2,3\ .\] (1.8.11)

**Proof** By Theorem 1.8.4 both sides of (1.8.11) define separately continuous trilinear maps

\[\prod_{j=1}^{3}{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\to{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X _{2}\times X_{3},E_{5})\ .\]

By (1.8.5), Remark 1.4.1(c), and Example 1.4.2(c) they coincide on the dense linear subspace \(\prod_{j=1}^{3}{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{j})\otimes E_{j}\), hence everywhere.
**(d)**: If \(u_{j}\in L_{1,\mbox{\scriptsize loc}}(X_{j},E_{j})\) then \(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}\in L_{1,\mbox{\scriptsize loc}}(X_{1}\times X_{2} ,E_{0})\) and

\[u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(x_{1},x_{2})=u_{1}(x_{1})\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2}(x_ {2})\qquad\mbox{for a.a.}\ (x_{1},x_{2})\in X_{1}\times X_{2}\ .\]

**Proof** This follows easily from (1.8.7) and the classical Fubini theorem.

---

**(e)**: _Distributivity_ Suppose that

are multiplications between Banach spaces, all denoted by \(\bullet\). Also suppose that

\[(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\bullet(e_{3}\bullet e_{4})=(e_{1}\bullet e_{3})\bullet(e_{2 }\bullet e_{4})\ ,\qquad e_{j}\in E_{j}\ ,\quad j=1,\ldots,4\ ,\]

and \(a_{j}\in{\cal E}(X_{j},E_{j})\) and \(u_{j}\in{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j+2})\), \(\ j=1,2\). Then

\[(a_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}a_{2})\bullet(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2})=(a_{1} \bullet u_{1})\otimes_{\bullet}(a_{2}\bullet u_{2})\ .\] (1.8.12)

ProofFirst we note that, thanks to (d), \(a_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}a_{2}\in{\cal E}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E_{0})\). Hence Theorems 1.8.4 and 1.6.4 guarantee that both sides of (1.8.12) are well-defined quadrilateral separately continuous maps from

\[{\cal E}(X_{1},E_{1})\times{\cal E}(X_{2},E_{2})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1}, E_{3})\times{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{2},E_{4})\]

into \({\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E_{8})\). It follows from (1.8.5) and (d) that they coincide on the dense linear subspace

\[\big{(}{\cal E}(X_{1})\otimes E_{1}\big{)}\times\big{(}{\cal E}(X_{2})\otimes E _{2}\big{)}\times\big{(}{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{1})\otimes E_{3}\big{)}\times \big{(}{\cal D}^{\prime}(X_{2})\otimes E_{4}\big{)}\ ,\]

hence everywhere.

**(f)**: Let \(F_{j}\), \(\ j=0,1,2\), be Banach spaces and suppose that

\[F_{1}\times F_{2}\to F_{0}\ ,\quad(f_{1},f_{2})\mapsto f_{1}\bullet f_{2}\]

is a multiplication. Also suppose that \(T_{j}\in{\cal L}(E_{j},F_{j})\), \(\ j=0,1,2\), satisfy

\[(T_{1}e_{1})\bullet(T_{2}e_{2})=T_{0}(e_{1}\bullet e_{2})\ ,\qquad e_{j}\in E _{j}\ ,\quad j=1,2\ ,\]

that is, the diagram

\(E_{1}\times E_{2}\)\(E_{0}\)\(T_{1}\)\(T_{2}\)\(F_{1}\times F_{2}\)\(F_{0}\)\(F_{1}\times F_{2}\)\(F_{0}\)\(F_{1}\times F_{2}\)\(F_{2}\times F_{3}\)\(F_{4}\times F_{5}\)\(F_{6}\times F_{7}\)\(F_{1}\times F_{2}\)\(F_{3}\times F_{4}\)\(F_{5}\times F_{6}\)\(F_{7}\times F_{8}\)\(F_{1}\times F_{2}\)\(F_{3}

---

is commutative. Then, given \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E}\}\), the diagram

is commutative as well.

**Proof** We have to show that

\[(T_{1}u_{1})\otimes_{\bullet}(T_{2}u_{2})=T_{0}(u_{1}\otimes_{\bullet}u_{2})\ , \qquad u_{j}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j},E_{j})\ ,\quad j=1,2\ .\]

From Remark 1.6.5(g) and Theorem 1.8.4 we infer that both sides of this equality define separately continuous bilinear maps that coincide on the dense linear subspace \(\big{(}\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\otimes E_{1}\big{)}\times\big{(}\mathfrak{F }^{\prime}(X_{2})\otimes E_{2}\big{)}\). Thus they are equal.

### Examples

Finally, we include a few simple examples demonstrating the usefulness of tensor products.

#### 1.8.6 Examples

**(a)** The Dirac distribution \(\delta\in\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n})\) on \(\mathbb{R}^{n}\) is the \(n\)-fold tensor product of the 'one-dimensional' Dirac distribution \(\delta\in\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R})\). Thus, in **symbolic notation**,

\[\delta(x)=\delta(x_{1})\otimes\delta(x_{2})\otimes\cdots\otimes\delta(x_{n})\ ,\qquad x=(x_{1},\ldots,x_{n})\in\mathbb{R}^{n}\ ,\]

where \(\delta(y):=\delta\in\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{m})\) for \(y\in\mathbb{R}^{m}\) and \(\otimes\) is the tensor product induced by the standard multiplication in \(\mathbb{K}\).

**(b)** Suppose that \(n=n_{1}+n_{2}\) with \(0\leq n_{1}\leq n-1\). Let \(X_{1}\) be open in \(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}\) and let \(X_{2}\) be a nonempty open cube in \(\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}}\). Also suppose that \(u\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) satisfies \(\partial_{j}u=0,\ \ n_{1}+1\leq j\leq n\). Then \(u=u_{1}\otimes 1_{X_{2}}\) for some \(u_{1}\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X_{1},E)\), where \(\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(\{0\},E):=E\). Lastly, \(u\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X,E)\) is constant if \(\partial_{j}u=0\) for \(1\leq j\leq n\) and \(X\) is connected.

**Proof** (i) First we consider the case \(n_{1}=0\) and \(n=1\). Thus \(X\) is a nonempty open interval in \(\mathbb{R}\) and \(u\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X,E)\) satisfies \(\partial u=0\). Fix any \(\varphi_{0}\in\mathcal{D}(X)\) with \(\langle 1,\varphi_{0}\rangle=1\). Then, given \(\varphi\in\mathcal{D}(X)\), put \(\psi:=\varphi-\langle 1,\varphi\rangle\varphi_{0}\in\mathcal{D}(X)\). Let

\[\chi(x):=\int_{-\infty}^{x}\psi(t)\,dt\ ,\qquad x\in\mathbb{R}\ ,\]

and observe that \(\chi\in\mathcal{D}(X)\). Consequently,

\[0=(\partial u)(\chi)=-u(\partial\chi)=-u(\psi)=\langle 1,\varphi\rangle u( \varphi_{0})-u(\varphi)\ ,\]

which shows that \(u=u(\varphi_{0})1_{X}\), that is, \(u\) is constant.

---

(ii) If \(Y_{j}\) are open subsets of \(\mathbb{R}^{m_{j}}\) for \(j=0,1,2\) and \(Y_{0}:=Y_{1}\times Y_{2}\), then \(\mathbf{1}_{Y_{0}}=\mathbf{1}_{Y_{1}}\otimes\mathbf{1}_{Y_{2}}\). Using this fact and induction, it suffices to consider the case \(n_{2}=1\).

Given \(\varphi_{1}\in\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\), it is easily verified that

\[u_{\varphi_{1}}:=\big{(}\varphi_{2}\mapsto u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2}) \big{)}\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X_{2},E)\ .\] (1.8.13)

By assumption, \(\partial u_{\varphi_{1}}=0\). Hence (i) implies the existence of \(e(\varphi_{1})\in E\) such that \(u_{\varphi_{1}}=e(\varphi_{1})\mathbf{1}_{X_{2}}\). Consequently,

\[u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=e(\varphi_{1})\langle\mathbf{1}_{X_{2}}, \varphi_{2}\rangle\ ,\qquad\varphi_{2}\in\mathcal{D}(X_{2})\ .\] (1.8.14)

Now fix \(\varphi_{2}\in\mathcal{D}(X_{2})\) with \(\langle\mathbf{1}_{X_{2}},\varphi_{2}\rangle=1\) and note that

\[u_{1}:=\big{(}\varphi_{1}\mapsto u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})\big{)}\in \mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X_{1},E)\ .\]

By (1.8.14) we see that \(u_{1}(\varphi_{1})=e(\varphi_{1})\) so that

\[u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=u_{1}(\varphi_{1})\langle\mathbf{1}_{X_{2}}, \varphi_{2}\rangle\ ,\qquad\varphi_{j}\in\mathcal{D}(X_{j})\ .\]

Now the assertion follows from Theorem 1.8.4.

(iii) If \(u\in\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X,E)\) satisfies \(\partial_{j}u=0\) for \(1\leq j\leq n\), we infer from (ii) that each point \(x\in X\) has a neighborhood \(U_{x}\) in \(X\) such that \(u\,|\,U_{x}=e_{x}\mathbf{1}_{U_{x}}\) for some \(e_{x}\in E\). If \(U_{x}\cap U_{y}\neq\emptyset\) then it follows from

\[e_{x}\langle\mathbf{1},\varphi\rangle=u(\varphi)=e_{y}\langle\mathbf{1}, \varphi\rangle\ ,\qquad\varphi\in\mathcal{D}(U_{x}\cap U_{y})\ ,\]

that \(e_{x}=e_{y}\). Let \(x\) and \(y\) be any two points in \(X\). Since \(X\) is connected there is a continuous path \(\gamma:\,[0,1]\to X\) connecting \(x\) and \(y\). Since \(\gamma([0,1])\subset\bigcup_{x\in X}U_{x}\) and \(\gamma([0,1])\) is compact and connected, we can find a finite chain \(U_{0},U_{1},\ldots,U_{m}\) of these neighborhoods covering \(\gamma([0,1])\) and satisfying \(U_{j-1}\cap U_{j}=\emptyset\). Then the above considerations imply that \(e_{x}=e_{y}\) for \(x,y\in X\), so that \(u=e\otimes\mathbf{1}_{X}\) for some \(e\in E\).
**(c)**: Let \(\Theta:=\chi_{\mathbb{R}^{+}}\in L_{1,\mathrm{loc}}(\mathbb{R})\) be the **Heaviside function**. Then

\[\chi_{P}:=\underbrace{\chi_{\mathbb{R}^{+}}\otimes\cdots\otimes\chi_{\mathbb{ R}^{+}}}_{n}\]

is the characteristic function of the natural positive cone \(P:=(\mathbb{R}^{+})^{n}\) of \(\mathbb{R}^{n}\). Since \(\partial\Theta=\delta\), we deduce from Remark 1.8.5(b) and from (a) that

\[\partial_{1}\cdots\partial_{n}\chi_{P}=\partial\chi_{\mathbb{R}^{+}}\otimes \cdots\otimes\partial\chi_{\mathbb{R}^{+}}=\delta(x_{1})\otimes\cdots\otimes \delta(x_{n})=\delta(x)\ .\]
**(d)**: Suppose that \(n=n_{1}+n_{2}\) with \(0\leq n_{1}\leq n-1\), and that \(u\in\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n},E)\) has its support in \(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}\times\{0\}\). Then there exist \(m\in\mathbb{N}\) and \(u_{\alpha}\in\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}},E)\) for \(\alpha\in\mathbb{N}^{n_{2}}\) with \(|\alpha|\leq m\) such that

\[u=\sum_{|\alpha|\leq m}u_{\alpha}\otimes\partial^{\alpha}\delta(x_{2})\ ,\qquad x _{2}\in\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}}\ .\]

This representation is unique.

---

**Proof** Since \(u\in{\cal E}^{\prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n},E)\), there exist \(m\in{\mathbb{N}}\) and \(K\subset\subset{\mathbb{R}}^{n}\) such that

\[|u(\varphi)|\leq cp_{m,K}(\varphi)\ ,\qquad\varphi\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n})\ .\]

Let \(\{\,\varphi_{\varepsilon}\ ;\ \varepsilon>0\,\}\) be a mollifier on \({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\). Then, putting \(\ell:=n_{2}\) and

\[\psi_{\varepsilon}:=\varphi_{\varepsilon/4}*\chi_{(\varepsilon/2){\mathbb{B}}^ {\ell}}\ ,\qquad\varepsilon>0\ ,\]

it is easily verified that \(\psi_{\varepsilon}\in{\cal D}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\,)\) satisfies \(\psi_{\varepsilon}(0)=1\), \(\ {\rm supp}(\psi_{\varepsilon})\subset\varepsilon{\mathbb{B}}^{n_{2}}\), and

\[\|\partial^{\alpha}\psi_{\varepsilon}\|_{\infty}\leq c(\alpha,n_{2}) \varepsilon^{-|\alpha|}\ ,\qquad\alpha\in{\mathbb{N}}^{n_{2}}\ ,\quad \varepsilon>0\ .\]

Thus, given \(\varphi_{j}\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{j}}\,)\), \(\ j=1,2\), we see that \(\varphi_{1}\otimes(1-\psi_{\varepsilon})\varphi_{2}\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n _{1}}\times{\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\,)\) has its support in \({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{1}}\times({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\,)^{\bullet}\). Consequently,

\[u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\psi_{\varepsilon}\varphi _{2})+u\big{(}\varphi_{1}\otimes(1-\psi_{\varepsilon})\varphi_{2}\big{)}=u( \varphi_{1}\otimes\psi_{\varepsilon}\varphi_{2})\ ,\qquad\varepsilon>0\ ,\]

thanks to \({\rm supp}(u)\subset{\mathbb{R}}^{n_{1}}\times\{0\}\). Hence we infer from (1.8.15) and (1.8.16) that

\[\eqalign{|u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})|&\leq cp_{m,K}(\varphi_{1}\otimes \psi_{\varepsilon}\varphi_{2})\cr&\leq c\max_{|\alpha_{1}|+|\alpha_{2}|\leq m} p_{K_{1}}(\partial^{\alpha_{1}}\varphi_{1})p_{\varepsilon{\mathbb{B}}^{\ell}} \left(\partial^{\alpha_{2}}(\psi_{\varepsilon}\varphi_{2})\right)\cr&\leq c \max_{|\alpha_{1}|\leq m}p_{K_{1}}(\partial^{\alpha_{1}}\varphi_{1})\sum_{| \beta|\leq m-|\alpha_{1}|}\varepsilon^{|\beta|-m+|\alpha_{1}|}p_{\varepsilon{ \mathbb{B}}^{\ell}}(\partial^{\beta}\varphi_{2})\ ,}\]

where \(K_{1}\) is the canonical projection of \(K\) into \({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{1}}\).

Now suppose that \(\partial^{\alpha}\varphi_{2}(0)=0\) for \(|\alpha|\leq m\). Then Taylor's theorem implies

\[|\partial^{\beta}\varphi_{2}(x_{2})|\leq\varepsilon^{m-|\alpha_{1}|-|\beta|} \sum_{|\gamma|=m-|\alpha_{1}|}p_{\varepsilon{\mathbb{B}}^{\ell}}\left(\partial ^{\gamma}\varphi_{2}\right)\,,\qquad\varepsilon>0\ ,\quad x_{2}\in\varepsilon{ \mathbb{B}}^{\ell}\ ,\]

for \(|\beta|\leq m-|\alpha_{1}|\) and \(|\alpha_{1}|\leq m\). Thus we deduce from (1.8.17) that

\[|u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})|\leq cp_{m,K_{1}}(\varphi_{1})p_{m, \varepsilon{\mathbb{B}}^{\ell}}\left(\varphi_{2}\right)\,,\qquad\varepsilon>0\ ,\]

for \(\varphi_{j}\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{j}}\,)\), \(\ j=1,2\), with \(\partial^{\alpha}\varphi_{2}(0)=0\) for \(|\alpha|\leq m\). Observe that the right-hand side of the last estimate tends to zero as \(\varepsilon\to 0\) thanks to \(\partial^{\alpha}\varphi_{2}(0)=0\) for \(|\alpha|\leq m\). Consequently,

\[u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=0\quad\hbox{for}\quad\varphi_{j}\in{\cal E}({ \mathbb{R}}^{n_{j}}\,)\qquad\hbox{with}\quad\partial^{\alpha}\varphi_{2}(0)=0 \ ,\quad|\alpha|\leq m\ .\]

Given any \(\varphi_{2}\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\,)\), Taylor's theorem gives

\[\varphi_{2}(x_{2})=\sum_{|\alpha|\leq m}{1\over\alpha!}\partial^{\alpha} \varphi_{2}(0)x_{2}^{\alpha}+\psi(x_{2})\ ,\qquad x_{2}\in{\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}}\ ,\]

---

where \(\psi\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{2}})\) satisfies \(\partial^{\alpha}\psi(0)=0\) for \(|\alpha|\leq m.\) Thus (1.8.18) implies

\[u(\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2})=u\Big{(}\varphi_{1}\otimes\sum_{|\alpha|\leq m }\frac{1}{\alpha!}\partial^{\alpha}\varphi_{2}(0)x_{2}^{\alpha}\Big{)}=\sum_{| \alpha|\leq m}(-1)^{|\alpha|}u_{\alpha}(\varphi_{1})\partial^{\alpha}\varphi_{2 }(0)\]

for \(\varphi_{j}\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{j}})\), where

\[u_{\alpha}(\varphi_{1}):=\frac{(-1)^{|\alpha|}}{\alpha!}u(\varphi_{1}\otimes x _{2}^{\alpha})\ ,\qquad|\alpha|\leq m\ .\]

Now Theorem 1.8.4 entails

\[u=\sum_{|\alpha|\leq m}u_{\alpha}\otimes\partial^{\alpha}\delta(x_{2})\]

with \(u_{\alpha}\in{\cal E}^{\prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{1}},E).\)

Finally, suppose that there are \(\widetilde{m}\in{\mathbb{N}}\) and \(\widetilde{u}_{\alpha}\in{\cal E}^{\prime}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{1}},E)\) such that

\[u=\sum_{|\alpha|\leq\widetilde{m}}\widetilde{u}_{\alpha}\otimes\partial^{ \alpha}\delta(x_{2})\ .\]

By replacing \(m\) and \(\widetilde{m}\) by \(\max\{m,\widetilde{m}\},\) we can assume that \(m=\widetilde{m}.\) Then

\[0=\sum_{|\alpha|\leq m}(u_{\alpha}-\widetilde{u}_{\alpha})\otimes\partial^{ \alpha}\delta(x_{2})(\varphi_{1}\otimes x^{\beta})=(-1)^{|\beta|}\beta!\,(u_{ \beta}-\widetilde{u}_{\beta})(\varphi_{1})\]

for \(|\beta|\leq m\) and \(\varphi_{1}\in{\cal E}({\mathbb{R}}^{n_{1}}).\) This proves the asserted uniqueness.

**Topological Tensor Products of Distributions**

Now we consider the special case of tensor products of a scalar and a vector-valued distribution.

**1.8.7 Theorem** _Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{{\cal E},{\cal S}\}.\) Then_

\[\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}\mathfrak{F}(X_{2 },E)=\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\ .\]

**Proof** Thanks to Corollary 1.8.2 it suffices to show that \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) induces on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\) the projective topology.

Given a continuous seminorm \(p\) on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) belonging to the families (1.1.3) and (1.1.7), respectively, it is easily verified that there exist continuous seminorms \(r\) on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\) and \(s\) on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E),\) respectively, such that

\[p(\varphi\otimes\psi)\leq r(\varphi)s(\psi)\ ,\qquad\varphi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1 })\ ,\quad\psi\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\ .\]

---

Hence, given a representation \(\sum\varphi_{j}\otimes\psi_{j}\) of \(z\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\), it follows that

\[p(z)\leq\sum p(\varphi_{j}\otimes\psi_{j})\leq\sum r(\varphi_{j})s(\psi_{j})\ .\]

This implies that \(p(z)\leq r\otimes_{\pi}s(z)\) for \(z\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\). Thus \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) induces on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\) a topology weaker than the projective topology.

Conversely, let \(r\) and \(s\) be continuous seminorms on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\) and \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\), respectively, belonging to the respective families (1.1.3) and (1.1.7), and let \(\sum\varphi_{j}\otimes\psi_{j}\) be a representation of \(z\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\). Observe that

\[\sum\langle\varphi^{\prime},\varphi_{j}\rangle\langle\psi^{\prime},\psi_{j} \rangle=\left\langle\varphi^{\prime},\left\langle\psi^{\prime},\sum\varphi_{j} \otimes\psi_{j}\right\rangle\right\rangle\ ,\ \ \ \ \ \varphi^{\prime}\in \mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\ ,\ \ \psi^{\prime}\in\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{2},E)\ .\]

Hence, cf. (1.4.7),

\[r\otimes_{\varepsilon}s(z)=\sup_{\varphi^{\prime}\in\mathfrak{B}^{0}_{\varepsilon }\atop\psi^{\prime}\in\mathfrak{B}^{0}_{\varepsilon}}\Bigl{|}\sum\langle \varphi^{\prime},\varphi_{j}\rangle\langle\psi^{\prime},\psi_{j}\rangle\Bigr{|} =r\Bigl{(}s\Bigl{(}\sum\varphi_{j}\otimes\psi_{j}\Bigr{)}\Bigr{)}\]

by the bipolar theorem, where \(\mathbb{B}_{r}\) is the open \(r\)-unit-ball in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\) and \(\mathbb{B}_{s}\) is the open \(s\)-unit-ball in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\). From this we infer the existence of a continuous seminorm \(p\) on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) such that \(r\otimes_{\varepsilon}s(z)\leq p(z)\) for \(z\in\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\). Thus \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)\) induces on \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\otimes\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\) a topology that is stronger than the injective tensor product topology. Since \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{1})\) is nuclear, the latter coincides with the projective topology (e.g. [17, Theorem 50.1(f)]).

**1.8.8 Corollary** : _If \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{E},\mathcal{S}\}\) then_

\[\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}\mathfrak{ F}^{\prime}(X_{2},E^{\prime})=\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E)^{\prime}\ .\]

**Proof** From Corollary 1.4.10 and Theorem 1.8.7 we know that

\[\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E^{\prime})=\mathfrak{F}(X_{1}\times X _{2},E)^{\prime}=\bigl{(}\mathfrak{F}_{1}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}} {{\otimes}}\mathfrak{F}(X_{2},E)\bigr{)}^{\prime}\ .\]

Hence the assertion follows from (1.4.16) and by applying Corollary 1.4.10 once more.

It should be remarked that

\[\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}\mathcal{D}(X_{2}) \neq\mathcal{D}(X_{1}\times X_{2})\]

as topological vector spaces, although these spaces are equal as vector spaces. Moreover,

\[\mathcal{D}^{\prime}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}\mathcal{ D}^{\prime}(X_{2})\neq\bigl{(}\mathcal{D}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}}{{ \otimes}}\mathcal{D}(X_{2})\bigr{)}^{\prime}\]

(cf. [10, chap. I, p. 95]).

---

#### Kernel Theorems

After these preparations we can prove some 'vector-valued kernel theorems':

**1.8.9 Theorem**: _Let \(E\) be a Banach space and let \(X_{j}\) be open in \(\mathbb{R}^{n_{j}}\), \(j=1,2\). Then_

\[\mathcal{E}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E) \cong\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(X_{1}),\mathcal{E}(X_ {2},E)\big{)}\ ,\] \[\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(X_{1}\times X_{2},E^{\prime}) \cong\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{E}(X_{1}),\mathcal{E}^{\prime}(X_ {2},E^{\prime})\big{)}\ ,\] \[\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}\times\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}},E) \cong\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{S}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}), \mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}},E)\big{)}\ ,\] \[\mathcal{S}^{\prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}\times\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}},E^ {\prime}) \cong\mathcal{L}\big{(}\mathcal{S}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{1}}),\mathcal{S}^{ \prime}(\mathbb{R}^{n_{2}},E^{\prime})\big{)}\ ,\]

_where \(\cong\) denotes the canonical toplinear isomorphism._

ProofThese assertions are immediate consequences of Theorems 1.4.8 and 1.8.7, and of Corollary 1.8.8.

For completeness we also include a proof of the 'classical' Schwartz kernel theorem for scalar distributions. To do this we rely on the following functional-analytical result:

**1.8.10 Lemma**: _Suppose that \(\mathfrak{F}\in\{\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E}\}\). Let \((u_{\alpha})\) be a net in \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\otimes_{\pi}\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{2})\). Then \((u_{\alpha})\) converges to zero iff \(\langle u_{\alpha},\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2}\rangle\to 0\), uniformly with respect to \(\varphi_{j}\) in bounded subsets of \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})\), \(j=1,2\)._

ProofLet \(F\) and \(G\) be complete LCSs such that \(F\) is nuclear. Then it follows from [23, Corollaries 1 and 2 to Theorem IV.9.4], for example, that a net \((v_{\alpha})\) converges in \(F\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}}G\) towards zero iff \(v_{\alpha}(f^{\prime}\otimes g^{\prime})\to 0\), uniformly with respect to \(f^{\prime}\) and \(g^{\prime}\) in equicontinuous subsets of \(F^{\prime}_{w^{\star}}\) and \(G^{\prime}_{w^{\star}}\), respectively. Put \(F:=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\) and \(G:=\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{2})\). Let \(B_{j}\) be a bounded subset of \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})\). Then \(B_{j}\) is weakly bounded, hence bounded in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})_{w^{\star}}=\mathcal{L}_{s}\big{(}\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X _{j}),\mathbb{C}\big{)}\), by the reflexivity of \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})\). Thus the uniform boundedness principle implies that \(B_{j}\) is equicontinuous in \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})_{w^{\star}}\). Thus if \((u_{\alpha})\) is a net in \(\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{1})\stackrel{{\sim}}{{\otimes}} \mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{2})\) converging towards zero, it follows from \(\big{[}\mathfrak{F}^{\prime}(X_{j})\big{]}^{\prime}_{w^{\star}}=\mathfrak{F}( X_{j})_{w^{\star}}\) that \(\langle u_{\alpha},\varphi_{1}\otimes\varphi_{2}\rangle\to 0\), uniformly with respect to \(\varphi_{j}\) in bounded subsets of \(\mathfrak{F}(X_{j})\), \(j=1,2\), as asserted.
